He got a close and comfortable shave. The three floating heads pivot independently so it easily shaves contoured areas like the chin.<br /><br />The pop-up trimmer works well, also, and cleaned up my son's sideburn area really nicely.<br /><br />This shaver cannot be rinsed out with water. Instead, you pop open the head and use the supplied brush to clean out under the heads. We are used to being able to clean our electric razors with water so with that in mind, this razor is probably best used as a travel razor because of it's compact nature. It might also be a nice gift for a young man who has just started shaving because it's very comfortable to use at a great price.

  175. This is an entry-level razor that shaves well, is light, quiet, and easy to use. I've been using Norelco for decades and this one is complimenting my 5825XL that I've had for about 15 years. This razor (the 6948) feels a bit cheap; both light and plasticy, compared to my old razor. It is more round and less contoured, so the fit in the hand isn't as natural. It isn't a big deal, but don't expect this to feel as nice as higher end Norelcos. This isn't \\"Father's day\\" or \\"graduation gift\\" quality.<br /><br />There are two issues I have with Norelco: One is the batteries. On my unit I've had to replace the rechargeable battery (NiCAD) at least three times using a soldering iron and replacement batteries from Radio Shack. The battery on this model is a better one (Nickel Metal Hydride, or NiMH) and I hope it lasts. But the instructions are very clear that you cannot use it only corded and you shouldn't drain it all the way often and you shouldn't charge for more than 8 hours (or less than 8 hours). So this appears to still be a bit finicky. I don't want to remember about my razor; can't the electronics monitor things and just turn it off or use the battery when it needs to be used? Do I have to remember to plug it in at night and unplug in the morning?<br /><br />The other thing that bugs me is their recommendation to change the blades every year. I certainly go two or three years without replacing blades and I've had very few problems. If I go too long the blades do begin to cause skin irriation, but the once a year is a very conservative estimate. Perhaps I have a lighter beard than most.<br /><br />If you search for Norelco razors you'll see that their main line up consists of the 6945, PT720, PT730, AT810, and AT830. The 6948 (the razor being reviewed) is not very prominent. Go to the [[ASIN:B006GQYSDC Amazon listing for the 6945 ]]and scroll to the bottom for a comparison of Norelco razors and you won't find the 6948.<br /><br />The 6945 has a Lithium Ion battery but doesn't have a pop-up trimmer. It is my understanding that the Li-Ion battery is the more advanced technology and less likely to memory and other issues. However a trimmer is also important, so both of these razors are a bit of a compromise.<br /><br />Despite it being double the price, I think the [[ASIN:B006GQYSGO PT730]] is worth a strong consideration for the following reasons:<br />- The shaving head quality is two levels above that of the 6945/8. The PT730 blade is \\"duel precision cut\\" and the \\"Super Lift & Cut System\\". I know these are mostly marketing terms, but there does appear to be real physical changes to the blade and it is nice to know you have the one used on the higher end devices.<br />- It has a trimmer and the Li-Ion battery (no compromise)<br />- The blade is easier to clean as you can run water through it.<br />- The quick charge feature is nice; if your razor is dead and you shave on the go, you can charge it for 3-minutes and get one shave out of it.<br /><br />The only downside is price, but it may not be that drastic a difference in the long run. Although the Amazon listing for the PT730 says to change the heads every year , the instructions at Phlips-Norelco site say \\"New! 24 months\\" for a change for the PT7XX series (and one year for the 69XX series). If you go by this, the razors will cost about the same over a two year period since the replacement heads cost about the same as the difference in cost for the razors. (The [[ASIN:B000068PBT replacement blades for the PT730]] are only five dollars more than [[ASIN:B004URZADG for the 69XX series]].)<br /><br />In summary, this is a very good simple razor at an excellent price and is a very good value. You might wish to check out a higher end model if this is your primary razor and plan to have it for several years.

After I'd been using it for two days I read the user manual, hoping that I'd find that Norelco had begun using a more easily replaceable battery. Instead, I found just the opposite: Norelco says that when the battery can no longer recharge, the owner should discard the battery properly and then THROW AWAY THE SHAVER!!!!<br /><br />The manual (page 19) says &#34;Do not attempt to replace the battery ... Discard your razor .. Do not attempt to plug the power cord into the outlet ... after the battery has been removed.&#34; There's no mention of taking it to a repair facility to replace the battery.<br /><br />This not only is environmentally and fiscally terrible practice, it means that Norelco probably has not designed this shaver to last much beyond the 30 month warranty. (the standard two year warranty is extended six months if you register online).<br /><br />On the positive side, it shaves better than I expected.   277. Somewhere on Amazon, in reply to a review or question, I stated that I've been satisfied with my ancient Norelco model 705RL but it was finally seeming kinda dull, and I'd simply like a new one just like it. This is it, except it's also cordless.<br /><br />I wasn't thrilled with everything being cordless -- suppose it runs out, I need a shave, and forgot to charge it? The good news is that this will also operate by using the cord. The bad news is that if you do that constantly, the battery life (as the instructions state) will be diminished. The good news is that if you use the cord only in emergencies, my guess is that any effect will be negligible.<br /><br />It has a pop-up trimmer. It's much, much more effective than the trimmer on my old Norelco -- that's probably just because of the old one's age (it used to work well). I also bought Norelco's basic groomer, but doubt I'll use it. The shaver's trimmer seems, while very effective, less aggressive than the groomer's (which also sounds louder, like a barber's trimmer). Which means if you're trimming a beard, the shaver allows a little margin for error.<br /><br />The shaver's sound is nicely muted, and compared to my old one, mechanically the old one sounds like Model T.<br /><br />I sometimes skip a day or three before shaving. Using a pre-shave lotion, this shaver has no problem catching me up. And if I let it go too long, I just start by using the pop-up trimmer, then finish up with this shaver.<br /><br />Although this shaver is not immersible, the blade head comes off completely (press a button and it lifts right off). I used to do this with my old shaver, and either slid out the blades and immersed the parts in alcohol, or simply held the assembly under the faucet. (Put a strainer over the drain!) Once dry, reassemble. This model's instructions don't say you can do this (or not), but I see no reason why an a occasional brush-out and rinse like this won't keep it clean, efficient, and sanitary.<br/><br />There's a 45-day Money-back guarantee, mainly aimed at former razor users but apparently valid for any user. (You pay to ship insured to them.)<br /><br />Instructions state to charge it for a full 8 hours, for 35 minutes' use. I don't use it every day, but the first charge has held okay for more than a week. Instructions state: \\"Battery performance is best if you recharge only when the batteries are (almost) completely empty. ... Continuously recharging or continuously using as a corded razor will reduce life of batteries. You may also shave using the power cord provided. This razor will not recharge while being used corded. Charging and recharging requires a full 8 hours. If razor has not been used for at least 1 month, razor must be recharged for a full 8 hours. ... Connect the charging plug into any 100V to 240V AC outlet. Use only the the power cord provided.\\" Outside North America, a plug adapter may be needed. The cord is a simple coiled cord (no power brick) that stretches comfortably from 18\\" to about 36\\". There is no low-charge or full-charge light, so make note of what time you plugged it in.<br /><br />Register your purchase online and you'll get an additional 6 months on the 2-year warranty.<br /><br />No doubt Norelco's more expensive models are cooler, and maybe they even shave better or something. But this does the job for me.

The cleaning procedure outlined in the manual is simple enough to follow and does a good job but the blades and foils are very delicate (e.g. tricky) so take your time.<br /><br />All in all, I'm delighted with this little shaver. I don't like shaving in the shower (never have) so a dry shaver is all I want, and this does that quite well.te (e.g. tricky) so take your time.<br /><br />All in all, I'm delighted with this little shaver.   343. Philips models 6948XL and AT830 are among the most useful of current rotary shavers. Both have articulated cutting heads in 3-head assemblies that are imbedded in shaver bodies rather than in floating holders. Both have internal batteries and wide, pop-up trimmers. Neither comes with a charging stand. A battery charge is rated to provide 35 minutes use with model 6948XL and 50 minutes use with model AT830.<br /><br />Value-priced model 6948XL has a nickel-metal-hydride battery, has cutting heads mounted in a fixed holder and is not waterproof, providing only dry shaving. It connects directly to AC power. Its internal power converter takes a rated 8 hours to charge the battery. There are no battery indicator lights, so users guess when the battery needs charging and time the charges themselves. Model 6948XL uses the older HQ56 heads.<br /><br />Intermediate-priced model AT830 has a lithium-ion battery, has cutting heads mounted in a rocking holder and is waterproof, allowing wet shaving. It comes with an external 15 volt, 5 watt AC-to-DC power converter that charges the battery in an hour or less. Indicator lights show when the battery needs charging and when it is fully charged. Model AT830 uses the newer HQ8 heads that provide somewhat closer shaves.<br /><br />The newer HQ8 heads each have two segments with fine, circular holes that are positioned toward the inside of a 3-head assembly. They are apparently intended to emulate the performance of foil shavers, handling short whiskers so that they are squarely cut. However, there are only 9 blades on an HQ8 cutter versus 15 blades on an older HQ56 cutter. To compensate, AT-series shavers rotate about 50 percent faster.<br /><br />Shave quality with model AT830 is good, if not quite as close as one gets from skillful use of a straight razor. It takes somewhat longer to get a uniform shave with model AT830 than with model 6948XL. Shave quality with model 6948XL is marginal, although it is better than one got with Norelco rotaries years ago. With either current Philips model, it takes less time to get uniform coverage of difficult neck and chin areas than it usually takes with a foil shaver.<br /><br />Philips rotaries have become value leaders among current electric shavers. Performance has improved over the Norelco rotary shavers of years ago--the brand Philips distributed in North America before the early 1980s. Philips currently offers models with good performance at premium, intermediate and value prices. Premium models have cutting heads mounted in floating holders and come with charging stands.<br /><br />I began using Remington electrics years ago, when they were the most reliable units of the day. In those days Norelco provided a shave with little skin irritation, but it was a fairly coarse shave with poor feel and appearance. Then Braun, while owned by Gillette, introduced titanium foil shavers that combined fairly close shaves with little skin irritation, and I switched to them.<br /><br />Unfortunately, foil shavers don't cope well with outlying areas of neck and chin, where whiskers tend to bend over and escape being clipped. The Braun triple-track design does better than just a curved foil, but it typically needs many passes to provide a uniform shave.<br /><br />With their high speeds, foil shavers don't really cut whiskers. They grind whiskers to powder, provided the whiskers can be persuaded through the holes in the surface of a foil. Currently Braun is delivering its best foil technology to the U.S. only at premium prices, encouraging another look at alternatives.<br /><br />Rotary shavers provide much of their action around the edges of disk-shaped \\"combs\\" where whiskers can slip through slots. Their low speeds encourage shaving with slower and more strategic motions. Because rotaries are quiet, one easily hears when cutters engage whiskers. Recent Philips models provide thinner combs and more precise mating of cutter blades to combs, as compared with Norelco models of years ago.<br /><br />Cleaning a rotary shaver appears more important than cleaning a foil shaver. Larger whisker fragments put drag on heads and internal parts. Removing head assemblies and brushing while dry has proved most effective, even though model AT830 can be washed with hot water. Philips does not offer cleaning accessories comparable to accessories from Braun. A few premium shavers have cleaning bases that can't be bought separately.<br /><br />Philips model AT830 is a good choice for everyday use at home. Overall, it performs as well or better than current foil shavers and provides uniform shaves somewhat faster. However, a little more time will be spent cleaning the shaver. Model 6948XL might be a good choice as a travel shaver. It's somewhat more rugged and won't cost as much to replace if lost or damaged.

  447. I've been shaving with an electric razor for about 20 years now. I've never liked using a blade and really like the speed an ease of use of an electric. For the first 5 years of shaving, I used a floating head type razor like what this Philips offers. I then switched to a foil type razor and haven't looked back, but I thought it would be worth re-visiting this type of razor to see if I would be willing to switch back. It's a tough call. This razor does offer a lot and does a great job at cutting facial hair, but I think I like the closeness of the foil type razor more. However, there is nothing wrong with this razor, and if you're looking for an inexpensive electric razor I really don't think you can go wrong here. Here are a few of my thoughts on this razor:<br /><br />It's quiet...very quiet. About 1/3 the volume of my foil razor. Since that doesn't really matter much to me, it wasn't a big factor in my overall decision. I guess I was just surprised a how quiet this razor is.<br /><br />The heads do a fine job cutting. I actually think this razor is slightly faster on the neck hairs (which as we all know are the hardest to get a close shave on) than my foil razor. But strangely enough I found shaving under the nose and chin my foil razor did a better job. I had some difficulty navigating this razor in tight areas like right under the nose. Still though, this razor did just fine.<br /><br />I do wish this razor had some sort of indicator that the battery was getting low. It has 1 light, green, that lights up when the razor is being charged. But it never tells you when it's fully charged, and never warns you when it's losing power and ready to recharge. My foil razor has a battery gauge that shows the % of battery life left which is incredibly handy, especially when traveling. However, given that my foil razor was 3x as much $ as this one, that's just a feature that you have to pay for. But I think this one could at least have the green light turn yellow, or blink or something to indicate it's time to charge.<br /><br />This razor is very light weight which is nice, but given the 3 heads, it's bulkier than my foil razor. Takes up a bit more room, especially when traveling.<br /><br />Overall, this is a fine product and it does it's job well. Of course you get what you pay for, and this is a bare bones product with not bells or whistles.yellow, or blink or something to indicate it's time to charge.<br /><br />This razor is very light weight which is nice, but given the 3 heads, it's bulkier than my foil razor. An important thing to note when reading reviews about shavers, razors, etc., is that everybody has different skin and hair types. What works for one person may not work for another.<br /><br />For me, this razor works. My skin isn't rough and my beard hairs aren't made of steel. I read a couple 1-star reviews from people saying using this razor was like holding a weedwhacker to their face and I can happily say that this is far from the case. It glides smoothly across my face, and like magic my facial hair disappears. I don't have any problem getting the &#34;hard to reach places&#34; around my jaw bones and under my neck, it works fine in those areas if I hold my skin taught and shave in gentle circles.<br /><br />I used to shave with disposable razors, so this is the first electric shaver I've ever used. It's so easy to use, and so much faster than a razor! The instructions say it may take up to three weeks for your skin to adjust but I can say that my skin has felt perfectly fine throughout the past week of use. In fact my skin would get far more irritated using a razor as opposed to this.<br /><br />It is a little inconvenient not having any sort of battery indicator other than a green light to show that its charging, but it's simple enough to just charge it overnight when it starts to wind down. The popup trimmer is pretty handy though, but I've only used it once.<br /><br />Since this is the first electric shaver I've ever used, and I'm a cheap college student, this thing is amazing to me. It doesn't feel cheap at all. That being said, I'm sure there are nicer ones out there, but I can't imagine how they could possibly be THAT much better than this because this one gives me a pretty damn close shave. In some areas of my neck, particularly spots that were hard to get at with a razor, this shaver outperforms the razor. In other areas, the razor did a better job. But overall, this thing cuts down shaving time by about 90%, and if it gives me a smooth enough shave for my girlfriend to be happy, then I'm happy.

  1044. This razor is pretty decent and gives a pretty close shave. The battery life is quite limited and eventually you may need to just plug it in. The head pops off and can be washed in hot water and the rest is easy enough to clear. One thing I finally figured out about these 3 head Norelco shavers: if you manage to get a few longer hairs into the blades they tend to wrap around and eventually impede the movement of the head and displace the edges enough to make the shave no longer close. Inside the shaver head, unscrew the little plastic thingy and the blade assemblies pop out. One by one, pop them out, remove the blade from it's little cowling and remove any long hair wrapped around or coiled around axle of blade wheel or blade, and replace in the head. Replace plastic screw top. If there was hair inside function should miraculously recover!

  1085. I'm an established adult male with many years of shaving experience. On a scale of 1 to 10 where 1 is the lightest and 10 is the heaviest beard, I'd say I have a 7. I grow hair on my face fairly fast and if I were a normal person, I would have to shave every day. I say it that way because I also have sensitive skin on my neck and if I shaved every day, I would literally destroy my neck, even with the most careful of shaves with the newest razor. So I shave once or twice a week followed up with a [[ASIN:B004QWST7Y beard trimmer]] to keep things acceptable until my next shave. When I do shave these days, I normally use a [[ASIN:B003KWO3UI Gillette Fusion Proglide]] with good [[ASIN:B0084GVSWG Italian shaving cream]] applied with a [[ASIN:B003WR3QSG badger hair shaving brush]]. I shave with a light touch and generally, only in the down direction. I finish up with a [[ASIN:B003LEXEDW RazoRock alum block]]. The whole method works great and I'm left with a close shave with almost no irritation, which is especially important for my neck.<br /><br />But I wanted something to supplement my cartridge shaves. Something quick and carefree.<br /><br />Enter the Phillips Norelco Rechargeable cordless razor, or so I thought.<br /><br />This Phillips-Norelco comes with a coiled cord which stretches out to about 6 feet when uncoiled, a cleaning brush and a protective cover for the shave heads. The device itself fits in the hand nicely, although it is a little top heavy. It's either on or off and the power switch is coated in non-slip rubber. Note that this particular razor is not waterproof. It as a pop-up beard trimmer on the back to trim sideburns and the like, but is not meant to groom a full beard. The three shave heads float individually so that they can more easily conform to the curves of the face - this is a compound mechanism - The three mounts each spring in towards the center and the three actual round blades float on them. It's very floaty.<br /><br />So I charged it up for eight hours and gave it a try on a three-day beard. Unfortunately, even though the device has a green light to indicate the battery is charging, it has no indication of a full charge or the charge state when using the device. I imagine such features are reserved for more expensive models. The shave started out normally. The razor was quieter than I expected, but it had sort of an unrefined grinding sound to it. I could feel the floaty heads floating. I did what I thought was a decent job, avoiding my sideburns and trying to keep light, even pressure and a circular motion. Unfortunately, right after I finished, I started to feel a burning sensation, especially around my lower neck. My lower neck started to get splotchy red, irritated and it burned a lot. I used my [[ASIN:B003LEXEDW RazoRock alum block]] to calm it down but it still burned for hours afterwards. Even worse, the splotchy red marks on my lower neck lasted for three days! That was despite daily applications of the [[ASIN:B003LEXEDW RazoRock alum block]] which usually works like a charm.<br /><br />Once nice thing was that most of my shaved beard was caught by the head assembly which pops off for easy cleaning. That's about the only good thing I can say about it so far.<br /><br />Okay, so my first experience with this didn't go well. I will try it again soon and report my findings. It's not like I'm new at shaving, but maybe I was using it wrong?it a try on a three-day beard.
